Round 4 reflection and concrete adjustments
What Round 4 revealed
- Anchors remain the backbone: Quill with Agent_1, Apple with Agent_2, Jewel with Agent_3. These anchors attract broad support and should stay fixed for durability.
- Stone and Pencil are the real levers between Agents 4 and 5. Moves involving Stone need a credible, group-wide payoff in Round 5 to be acceptable; otherwise Stone stays with the holder who values it most (Agent_5 in many rounds).
- Round 4 proposals mostly failed to gain unanimous acceptance because they either moved Stone away without a credible compensation or bundled too many changes, risking anchor stability.
Compatibilities and conflicts
- Compatible: The anchors (Quill, Apple, Jewel) are widely supported across proposals; Agent_1, Agent_2, and Agent_3 align well on seed-based distribution.
- Conflicting: Stone and Pencil entre Acts between 4 and 5 drive most contention. Moves away from Stone’s current holder (Agent_5) require credible, multi-agent benefits and a forward plan that includes Round 5.
- Observed pattern: Proposals that keep Path A baseline tend to do better in acceptance; moves toward Path B require a pre-committed compensation path to a future round.
Blockers to consensus
- The main blocker is Stone’s position. Any shift of Stone needs a transparent Round 5 payoff that benefits multiple agents and preserves anchors.
- Moves that disrupt seed integrity or hoard top value for a single agent struggle to gain broad support.
Concrete adjustments to improve consensus (actionable steps)
1) Lock in Round 4 Path A as the working baseline and run a tight Move 1 concession test:
- Move 1 (bounded): Swap Stone and Pencil (Stone to Atom_4, Pencil to Atom_5) for Round 4. This is a narrow test to see if a small coalition could form around rebalancing the levers.
- Timebox: 12–15 minutes to decide whether Move 1 passes or fails.
2) If Move 1 passes (credible coalition forms):
- Adopt Move 1 for Round 4.
- Immediately publish a concrete Round 5 compensation plan that preserves anchors (Quill/A1, Apple/A2, Jewel/A3) and yields tangible gains for multiple agents. Examples of such gains could include a future adjustment that improves Stone or Pencil for a coalition beneficiary, or a small offsetting concession elsewhere that benefits the group.
3) If Move 1 fails (no coalition):
- Maintain Path A for Round 4.
- In Round 5, implement a refined compensation framework focused on broader alignment without moving anchors. This could be a targeted Pencil-for-Jewel or Pencil-for-Apple swap tied to a clear, shared benefit, or another small concession that broadens multi-agent gains.
4) Round 5 readiness (if Path B is ever pursued):
- Any Move B in Round 4 must be accompanied by a written Round 5 plan that:
  - Keeps Quill with A1, Apple with A2, Jewel with A3 fixed.
  - Delivers tangible gains to multiple agents (not just the movers).
  - Is agreed in advance by all parties.
Suggested messaging for quick progress
- Agent_5 (you): “Let’s lock Round 4 Path A as the baseline and run Move 1 (Stone↔Pencil) in a 12–15 minute window. If a credible coalition forms, we publish a Round 5 compensation plan immediately. If not, we proceed with Round 4 as baseline and prepare Round 5 refinements that respect seeds.”
- Agent_4/Agent_5 (for Move 1): “We’re testing a bounded Stone↔Pencil swap; if it forms a coalition, we’ll accept Move 1 and we’ll outline a Round 5 plan that delivers broad gains while preserving anchors.”
- Agent_3 (Jewel’s holder): “I stay anchored to Jewel; any Move B must come with a robust Round 5 compensation that distributes benefits beyond the movers.”
Round 3 recap in one line
- The clear path to quick consensus is to protect anchors, test a narrow Stone↔Pencil swap, and then secure a credible Round 5 compensation plan that yields multi-agent gains if Move 1 passes.
Proposed Round 5 horizon (high level)
- Anchors fixed: Quill/A1, Apple/A2, Jewel/A3.
- Levers: Stone/A5 and Pencil/A4 remain the active levers for Coalition 4 and 5.
- Gains: A tangible, multi-agent improvement (e.g., a small compensating tweak that benefits at least two non-mover agents) with explicit timelines.
- Communication: Draft and share the Round 5 plan in advance so everyone knows the payoff path before any Round 4 moves finalize.
